## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / batch-reactor ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by chemical kinetics via rate laws (mass-action and empirical forms). With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are single-species decay/production ODEs with concentration-dependent order and possibly time-varying effective rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production, e.g., surface-limited)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, many decompositions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or A+A processes)
- n-th order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global order kinetics)
- General polynomial mass-action surrogate: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (net source + multiple pathways lumped)
- Parallel pathways lumping: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order loss channels)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-like kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth limited by depletion/carrying capacity c1)
- Saturating/inhibited effective rate (empirical): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to site limitation/inhibition lumping)
- Time-varying rate constant (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (slow change in conditions, e.g., catalyst activation/deactivation approximated linearly)
- Time-varying rate constant (exponential deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective activity decays with time, common in catalyst deactivation)
- Induction/activation factor: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (slow turn-on of reactive pathway or mixing/heat-up transient)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Mass-action orders: appearance of A, A**2, A**n in dA_dt suggests elementary/overall reaction order and collision-based kinetics.
- Reversibility/equilibrium: a term proportional to (A - c) indicates relaxation toward a steady-state/equilibrium concentration set by other (unmodeled) species or chemostatting.
- Multiple pathways: sums like -c0*A - c1*A**2 indicate parallel reactions with different molecularities contributing additively to net rate.
- Autocatalysis: factors like A*(c - A) or A*(c + A) indicate self-accelerating kinetics with eventual limitation, common in chain/autocatalytic systems.
- Catalyst deactivation/aging: multiplying a concentration-dependent rate by exp(-c*t) (or similar monotone decay in t) reflects loss of activity over runtime.
- Induction periods: prefactors such as (1 - exp(-c*t)) (or other increasing functions of t) capture delayed onset due to activation, inhibitor consumption, or mixing/thermal equilibration.
- Saturation/inhibition in a single-variable surrogate: rational forms A/(A + c) or A/(c + A**n) represent finite-capacity effects (sites, radicals) even when other species are not explicitly modeled.
- Baseline source/sink: a constant term c0 in dA_dt suggests external feed, background generation, or an offset from imperfect centering/hidden species pools.

GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_p*sin(c3*A)
Candidate formulas: 59

GT is the fixed function of two variables
\[
f(t,A)= -0.3122128845632889\,A\,e^{-0.07984001873836775\,t}\;+\;0.4717280564351947\,\sin(0.8721876285304352\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must be exactly “(constant)\(\cdot A\cdot e^{(constant)\,t\)” plus “(constant)\(\cdot \sin((constant)\,A)\)” with **no extra dependence on \(A\) or \(t\)** (no offsets, no extra rational/log/tanh/etc terms), and the sine must have **zero phase shift** (no “\(+c4\)” inside).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can set its free constants to reduce it exactly to the GT form and then match coefficients/exponents.

---

### 1. `A*c0/(A + c1) + A*c2/(A + c3) + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6*sin(A*c7 + c8)`
Has two rational-in-\(A\) terms \(A/(A+c)\) that cannot be made identically 0 for all \(A\) except by setting their numerators to 0: set \(c0=0\) and \(c2=0\). Then we have \(A*c4 e^{c5 t} + c6\sin(A c7 + c8)\). This can match GT if we also set \(c8=0\) and choose \(c4,c5,c6,c7\) appropriately. **Matchable.**

### 2. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5`
To match GT, constant offset must be 0 ⇒ \(c5=0\). Also need no phase shift in sine ⇒ \(c4=0\). Then it becomes \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + c2\sin(A c3)\), which can match by choosing \(c0=-0.3122...\), \(c1=-0.07984...\), \(c2=0.4717...\), \(c3=0.8721...\). **Matchable.**

### 3. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4)`
Need \(c4=0\). Then same as above. **Matchable.**

### 4. `... + c5 + c6*log(A*c7 + 1)*log(c8*t + 1)`
Extra term must vanish for all \(A,t\). Easiest: set \(c6=0\). Also set \(c5=0\), \(c4=0\). Remaining matches as in (2). **Matchable.**

### 5. `... + c5 + tanh(A*c6)`
Need \(c5=0\). Need tanh term to vanish for all \(A\): set \(c6=0\) so \(\tanh(0)=0\). Also set sine phase \(c4=0\). Then matches. **Matchable.**

### 6. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2 + c3 + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6)`
GT has no \(A\) linear term without exponential ⇒ must set \(c2=0\). No constant offset ⇒ \(c3=0\). No sine phase shift ⇒ \(c6=0\). Then becomes \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + c4\sin(A c5)\) and can match. **Matchable.**

### 7. `... + c7*tanh(A*c8)`
As in (6), set \(c2=0\), \(c3=0\), \(c6=0\). Also must remove tanh term: set \(c7=0\) (or \(c8=0\) gives constant \(\tanh(0)=0\) anyway). Then matches. **Matchable.**

### 8. `... + c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7`
Need log term gone ⇒ \(c5=0\). Need constant offset gone ⇒ \(c7=0\). Need sine phase \(c4=0\). Then matches. **Matchable.**

### 9. `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2/(A + c3) + c4*sin(A*c5 + c6) + c7`
Rational term must vanish ⇒ set \(c2=0\). Constant offset ⇒ \(c7=0\). Sine phase ⇒ \(c6=0\). Then matches. **Matchable.**

### 10. `... + c5*tanh(A) + c6`
Need tanh term gone ⇒ \(c5=0\). Need constant offset gone ⇒ \(c6=0\). Need sine phase \(c4=0\). Then matches. **Matchable.**

### 11. `A*c0/(A + c1) + A*c2 + A*c3 + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(A*c8 + c9)`

Also need no sine phase ⇒ \(c9=0\). Then we have \(A c4 e^{c5 t} + c6\sin(A c8)\) which matches. **Matchable.**
